After 2:00 PM yesterday, foreign taxpayers arrived one after another, with a constant flow of vehicles and horses. The police force also dispatched additional Western officers and detectives to the scene to maintain order. By 2:30 PM, a large number of taxpayers had arrived, and the meeting was declared open. Mr. Baker was publicly elected as chairman, followed by the election of a secretary. After the meeting rules were approved as usual, the agenda was discussed, with details as follows:

Item 4: In his speech on Item 4, the Chairman of the Board said, "In my capacity as the retiring Chairman of the Board, I propose the fourth resolution, which is to pass the report on the accounts for 1931. The annual report for this year is quite lengthy, and part of it has already appeared in the newspapers, so I will not go into further detail here. However, Shanghai has recently gone through a period of crisis. Fortunately, the defense forces of various countries, the merchant corps, and the special police came forward to maintain order, and many residents of the concession also assisted in a personal capacity. I must express the sincere thanks of the Municipal Council on their behalf. The diligence of the council's staff is also commendable. The financial report for 1931 has already been distributed and does not need to be elaborated on. The ordinary budget actually had a surplus of more than 350,000 taels, which was unexpected. This was due to strenuous efforts to tighten spending and the improvement in silver prices, as well as the allocation of funds between the ordinary and temporary budgets. The temporary budget had a deficit of more than 510,000 taels. The temporary expenditures for this year included the repayment of the 1921 Eight Percent Loan, as well as the purchase of land for parks costing 800,000 taels, and the widening and extension of roads costing 2.7 million taels. Most of these temporary expenses were paid for with the proceeds from the sale of the Electricity Department. Regarding the

Political Situation: The Public Concession has recently experienced a severe crisis unprecedented in its history. The full impact and causal relationships are not yet clear. During and after the war, the Board of Directors, in view of the international nature of the concession, made every effort to maintain neutrality and impartiality, while simultaneously maintaining its administrative authority. This was not easy at a time when the emotions of most citizens were running high. The Municipal Council had to uphold everything from a legal standpoint. At that time, some people advocated that the Council should take extraordinary measures, which the Council could not satisfy, and therefore was inevitably subject to criticism. The Municipal Council had to maintain its administration and avoid falling into traps, so it had to pay close attention to everything every day, and also had to take into account national sentiments at all times to avoid causing incidents due to suppression. Fortunately, the Council did not offend the feelings of the Chinese and Japanese residents during this period, which is something that the retiring Board of Directors can be gratified about. The responsibilities of the new Board of Directors are extremely heavy, and finance is one of the major challenges. The Council's finances have always been a difficult issue. Now, after the chaos, commerce and industry have suffered huge losses, so the difficulties will naturally be even greater. However, the Public Concession has gone through several difficult times and has always recovered quickly, so there is reason to be optimistic about the future. However, the restoration of the original state may take longer. The financial problem is only one of the problems. Shanghai is at the forefront of Sino-foreign relations, and there is a (Shanghai problem). There are many inconsistencies in the administrative system of this city, and after this chaos, several weaknesses have been exposed. Whenever there is an international conflict, Shanghai is subject to various dangers. Therefore, the relevant powers must immediately pay close attention to the current and future political status of Shanghai. The Municipal Council has no power to direct the path to be taken regarding the future status of Shanghai. However, I believe that future international conferences will discuss this issue, and they will inevitably have to discuss it. The Municipal Council will then have the opportunity to fully contribute its opinions based on its experience and knowledge, in order to be adopted as much as possible. The permanent solution to the Shanghai problem must also take into account the interests of both Chinese and foreigners. This is also a fact that must be fully acknowledged. The new Board of Directors will do its best to achieve this goal, which the taxpayers can rest assured of. Regarding the Shanghai

Page 5

Special District Court: At last year's annual meeting, regarding the

Special District Court's criminal section, I said that apart from the Nanjing government's attempts to interfere in communist cases, there was not much that could be criticized about the Municipal Council's handling of criminal cases in the Special District Court. This situation has not changed much. However, since mid-September, when the boycott of Japanese goods began, cases involving Japanese goods and anti-Japanese issues have become lawless. In addition to a large number of propaganda materials and inspections, Chinese goods labeled as Japanese goods, worth more than 600,000 yuan, were forcibly seized, and a large part of them were sold. The proceeds were also disposed of without authorization. Several Chinese businessmen labeled as traitors were illegally arrested and detained in the Tianhou Temple and other places. All kinds of acts were carried out as if laws and regulations did not exist. The Special District Court, either due to a misguided sense of patriotism or out of fear of violence, simply turned a blind eye to everything, making it impossible for the Municipal Council to deal with these incidents. This attitude of the Special District Court was undoubtedly one of the causes of the Sino-Japanese war in Zhabei. In this emergency situation, the Special District Court was negligent, which has fundamentally shaken, although not completely destroyed, the hope of foreign residents that the Chinese government could establish a court within the Public Concession that foreigners could trust. The current Special District Court is based on an agreement between the Chinese government and certain countries, starting on April 1, 1930, for a period of three years. If both parties agree, the term can be extended. This negotiation was conducted in secret at the time, but the Municipal Council's representatives were hastily consulted on certain points. Apart from this, the Municipal Council and foreign residents were completely unaware of the content until it became a *fait accompli*, which caused great resentment among the public. The reason why the negotiation was so secret and hasty at the time has not been officially announced, but given the political situation at the time, the relevant powers probably believed that it was better to have an agreement, no matter how unsatisfactory, than to have no agreement at all. Foreign businessmen are very dissatisfied with the civil aspects of the court, as can be seen from the annual speech of the president of the Harmony Business Association a month ago. Previously, the Municipal Council was not very concerned about civil cases in the court, but in light of recent events, it is also questionable how the court will legally enforce the municipal rates. Normally, negotiations should be started as soon as possible regarding the continuation of the court agreement or the revision of a more satisfactory new agreement. With the current dissatisfaction rising from all sides, and the new directors having declared that they will do their best to find a solution to this problem, it is hoped that a definite achievement can be made within a reasonable period of time. As far as foreign public opinion is concerned, the most satisfactory solution would be to establish an international court within the concession, applying uniform civil and criminal laws to all residents, regardless of nationality. There is almost unanimous agreement with this view, but in fact, we must completely leave these issues to the disposal of the relevant governments. Unless we obtain their sympathy and support, we cannot achieve anything in reforming or improving the local Chinese court. The practical difficulties in seeking a satisfactory solution to this matter are undoubtedly extremely significant, but not impossible. It is hoped that the new Board of Directors will devote themselves to this and achieve considerable success. Although the Chinese directors do not participate in my comments on the Special District Court, in the past year, the Chinese directors have assisted the Board of Directors in resolving many difficult issues, especially in the past few months. Their service to the concession has been extraordinarily valuable, which I am happy to commend.

Educational Affairs: Last year, I reported that 150,000 taels had been allocated to subsidize non-council schools. The detailed regulations have been drafted and announced, and it has been decided to subsidize foreign children's schools by 45% and Chinese children's schools by 55%. The former has already been allocated and will be issued soon. The latter cannot be allocated at the same time because the agreement with the Shanghai Municipal Education Authority

has not yet been reached. However, there has been progress in this agreement recently, and it is hoped that it can be handled simultaneously in 1932. Last year, it was reported that the Council had approved an education plan to add two Chinese children's primary schools every year before 1938, and two Chinese girls' middle schools before 1934. However, due to difficulties in buying land and economic reasons, the first year's program could not be fully implemented, or it may have to be slowed down in the future. Zizi Middle School and Primary School have rented buildings and opened one school each, and two existing primary schools are under construction. A foreign children's school has also been started construction.

Factory Regulations: In December 1929, the Nanjing government promulgated a Factory Law, which was later scheduled to take effect on August 1 of last year. This law is very broad in scope, and all economic and social aspects are worth discussing. From the perspective of the history of factory regulations, the current law is difficult to implement in China's current situation. At most, it can only be implemented slowly and gradually in order to suit China's economic and social progress. However, if part of this law can be implemented within the concession, Chinese and foreign factory owners will be very welcome, which can improve the conditions of workers in the concession. The conditions in certain factories are almost unspeakable. Also, if it is implemented, it is best to treat Chinese and foreign factories equally. However, foreign factory owners who enjoy consular jurisdiction are not bound by the Chinese Factory Law, and the factory laws of countries that have consular jurisdiction treaties with China have never been applied to their overseas Chinese citizens. Therefore, if the Municipal Council wants to exercise jurisdiction over factories in the concession, it must amend By-law 34 so that factories can be licensed, and the licensing regulations can include various rules deemed suitable for implementation in the Chinese government's Factory Law. However, amending the by-laws requires convening a special taxpayers' meeting, and one-third of the total number must be present. The Board of Directors originally intended to convene this special meeting before the annual meeting, but in view of the recent industrial situation and the closure of factories, with many workers losing their jobs as a result, it was decided to convene it when the situation is better. However, the Board of Directors will not shelve this matter, which taxpayers and the public can rest assured of. I now propose the fourth motion, which is to pass the annual report and final accounts for the year ending December 31, 1931. This motion was seconded by Mr. Bell, and the chairman put it to a vote, which was unanimously approved by the meeting.

Item 5: In his speech on Item 5, the Chairman of the Board said, "Before presenting the budget, there are several points to be explained. First, the ordinary budget and the education budget have now been separated. The ordinary expenses for education are roughly the same as last year, and the amount currently used for foreign children and Chinese children is also roughly the same. However, if the plan approved last year is carried out, the expenses for Chinese children's education should increase in the future. The current ordinary expenses for education are more than 1.38 million taels, which is about 1.74 percent of the municipal rates and land tax. Whether a certain amount of municipal revenue should be designated for this expense should be seriously considered. The explanation attached to the budget compares the figures for 1932 with those for 1931. Due to austerity and the recovery of the pound, it has been possible to keep the expenses of various departments roughly the same as last year. The Municipal Council is not a static organization, and its various functions are becoming increasingly complex. In the midst of the global commercial recession, it is not easy to maintain efficient administration with the same level of spending as last year. As for the revenue side, last year there was a surplus of about 2.3 million taels from the previous year, so the 1931 budget was balanced. This year, however, there is only a surplus of 350,000 taels from last year, and interest income has decreased significantly due to the gradual allocation of the proceeds from the sale of the Electricity Department. The ordinary budget for this year showed a shortfall of about 2.5 million taels from the outset. Normally, taxes should be increased

Page 6

to compensate. However, for various reasons, the plan to increase taxes had to be postponed, and other methods were adopted. After careful deliberation, there is still a shortage of about 1.25 million taels. It has recently been decided to sell some of the Council's surplus land. In addition to returning the original value to the temporary budget, the remaining balance will be transferred to the ordinary budget. However, although this measure is sound in principle, it is not sustainable in the long run. Therefore, an increase in taxes will be unavoidable in the near future. The temporary budget is estimated at more than 18.9 million taels, of which about 10 million taels are for debt repayment, and the remaining uses are also unavoidable. On the income side, in addition to allocating 16 million taels from the proceeds of the power company and about 1.5 million taels from the sale of land, it is still necessary to raise debt or raise funds by other means, not exceeding 2 million taels. In this way, about 88,000 taels can be left over at the end of the year to be carried over to the next year. I now propose the fifth motion, which is (to approve and adopt the expenditure for the year 1932 proposed by the current Board of Directors and the attached recommendations, and to authorize the Municipal Council to levy and collect the proposed taxes and fees, and to authorize it to raise no more than 2 million taels by appropriate means to meet the needs of the temporary budget). This motion was seconded by Mr. Bell, and the chairman put it to a vote, which was unanimously approved by the meeting.

Item 6: In his speech on Item 6, the Chairman of the Board said, "Regarding the issue of Chinese property committee members, last year, the Chinese directors and various Chinese organizations requested the Municipal Council to find a way to add two Chinese property committee members to the existing committee of three foreign members. The request was very urgent. A large part of the land in the concession is owned by Chinese, so the Municipal Council considers this request reasonable and feels that there should be no major opposition from foreign taxpayers. However, this matter requires amending the property regulations, and as usual, a special meeting of taxpayers should be convened. However, judging from past experience, it is difficult to obtain the legal quorum of one-third of the taxpayers except for extremely important events. However, there is another way to amend the property regulations. Taxpayers can authorize the annual meeting and order the Municipal Council to submit this matter to the relevant countries. If they adopt it, it can also be amended, just like the resolution of a special meeting. I now propose the sixth motion, which is (This meeting believes that it is appropriate to add two Chinese property committee members. The Board of Directors is hereby authorized to propose to the relevant countries to add two Chinese members to the Land Committee.) This motion was seconded by Mr. Bell, and the chairman put it to a vote, which was unanimously approved by the meeting. Mr. Baker was also elected as a land committee member.

Advocating Mutual Assistance and Cooperation Between Chinese and Western Taxpayers

Studying and Resolving the Joint Defense of the Concession in the Future

The Citizens' Federation, the United Federation of Commercial Circles, various branch associations, and the guilds of transportation, customs declaration, copper and iron, machinery, woolen mills, antique shops, embroidery, and other industries, as well as the United Federation of Ten-Person Patriotic Groups, and more than 100 other organizations, issued a declaration yesterday stating that, "The history of Shanghai in 1932, before today, already has countless pages of tragic records. The current facts tell us that this Japanese committee member, who is responsible for maintaining the security of the concession, not only abandoned his responsibility, but also personally destroyed the security. Here, we cannot but blame the previous Board of Directors of the Municipal Council. They failed the Chinese and Western taxpayers and made a mistake in their entrustment. Do we really want to blame the previous Board of Directors? We know that they had no malicious intent when entrusting them. We do not see the subsequent struggles of Major General MacNaghten, the previous Chairman of the Board. Although various struggles did not have an effect in the past, we should admit that they have fulfilled their considerable responsibility in a calm and peaceful manner. The previous Board of Directors has transferred the unfinished responsibility to the current Board of Directors. We must directly urge the Chinese directors and indirectly urge the Western directors to take on the responsibility in order to maintain and revive the Shanghai prosperity that is already in danger. On the other hand, in light of the past lessons, we should directly awaken the Chinese taxpayers and indirectly awaken the Western taxpayers to do their best to assist the Board of Directors and support the Municipal Council owned by the Chinese and Western taxpayers, because the Chinese and Western taxpayers are the masters of the concession today. The Chinese and Western taxpayers also cannot but bear the responsibility for the unprecedented catastrophe that the concession has suffered in the past. Looking at the past facts, we know that the protagonist of the tragedy that destroyed the prosperity was the Japanese soldier who acted on Japan's policy towards China, but who invited this protagonist to perform, and who witnessed this protagonist leaving the dignity of the rule of law, the principle of mutual assistance and cooperation, and the security maintenance program, and performing a tragedy that Chinese and Western taxpayers did not want to see or like, and was unable to stop it? They are all bound by the organizational law of the Defense Force Committee left over from the past. May I ask whether this kind of restraint should be liberated, whether this kind of organizational law can still be applied now, and whether it can continue to be used after the facts prove that it is not applicable? All Chinese and Western taxpayers who agree that the spirit of the rule of law is the basis for the administration of the Municipal Council, and who recognize that mutual assistance and cooperation between China and the West is sufficient to develop Shanghai's prosperity, must feel that the organizational law of the Defense Force Committee, which is not applicable, does need to be amended, and that the Defense Force Committee members who violate the wishes of the Chinese and Western taxpayers, plunder the political power of the Municipal Council, infringe on the rights of the Chinese and Western taxpayers, and destroy Shanghai's prosperity, need to be deprived of their future right of joint defense. For the sake of Shanghai's prosperity and the common happiness of the Chinese and Western taxpayers, standing on the position of the taxpayers, we advocate amending the organizational law of the Defense Force Committee and depriving the Japanese army of the right of joint defense in the future. Under this proposition, we have decided to do our best to struggle, choose a legal and reasonable way to meet the needs of maintaining and reviving the Shanghai prosperity that is already in danger. We hope that the representative assembly that accepts our commission will earnestly fulfill their responsibilities, and we also hope that all taxpayers in today's assembly, as well as fair Japanese taxpayers, will express warm sympathy for our proposition, and also rise up to organize a representative assembly to study the organizational law of the Defense Force Committee in the future and solve the joint defense problems in the concession in the future.

International Senior Pistol Championship Semi-Finals: Li Gongying Shows His Skills 14

Defeating Bernal to Win the Finals Qualification

Result: 1000 Points vs. 902 Points

Li Gongying, who once set a record for Chinese in the International Senior Pistol Championship, faced Bernal in the semi-finals yesterday afternoon at 5:30. In the first half, Li took the lead with 500 points to 464. The second half started at 9:00 and ended at 11:30, taking four and a half hours. He fired 118 times and finally defeated the strong enemy with 1000 points to 902, winning the finals qualification.

Bernal was also one of the past champions, and his technique and experience were no less than Li's. Therefore, he tried to strike Li in many ways during the competition. In the second half, when the difference was 140 points, he made several fierce advances and took the lead with 754 points to 748. If he could have maintained his normal state and continued unabated, it would have been difficult for Li to catch up. However, Li had real skills, coupled with continuous efforts, and he rose sharply with huge scores such as 35, 53, and 32, winning with 1000 points to 902. From an overall perspective, both of them suffered from stage fright, and their performance was greatly reduced compared to their usual scores. Li's largest scores were 76, 46, 33, 40, 40, 52, 30, 35, 53, and 32. Bernal's were 98, 42, 66, 43, and 43. Li averaged about 8 points per shot.

Attached are the results of the second week:

(1) Li Gongying defeated Shen Lince 1000 to 613

(2) Bernal defeated Lei Miti 1000 to 580

(3) Boerge defeated Clark 1000 to 929

(4) Medi Na defeated Nie Kaoer 1000 to 637

Shanghai Continues to Collect Various Grain Taxes 16

Limited to April 16th to May 15th

Due to the impact of the Shanghai war, the Shanghai County's various grain taxes for the 20th year were previously approved by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance to be temporarily postponed, and collection would resume when the people's minds were slightly settled, with a limit of one month, and penalties would be waived. Now that the situation is gradually easing, the County Finance Bureau has decided to set up a counter to collect taxes from the 16th of this month to the 15th of May, with a limit of one month, and penalties will be waived within the limit. In addition to reporting to the Department of Finance, a notice was issued to all grain households in Kaiyi yesterday, informing them to quickly pay off the various grain taxes for the 20th year within the limit to ensure their livelihood, and not to wait and see and delay themselves.

Jiangsu Flood Relief Association Concludes 18

Yesterday afternoon at 4 p.m., the Jiangsu Flood Relief Association held its sixth regular meeting in the back hall of the Renji Hall on Six Malu. Commissioners Wang Yiting, Huang Hanzhi, Du Yuesheng, Cheng Xiangqing, Wu Yunzhai, Lu Shaoliu, Gu Xinyi, and over ten others attended. All emergency winter relief efforts are coming to an end, and we should discuss how to plan the association's affairs from now on. Commissioner Cheng Xiangqing reported on the emergency winter relief situation, as well as the income and expenditure of relief funds. The committee received 82,000 yuan allocated from the Relief Committee, 338,000 yuan allocated from the Provincial Relief Committee, 364,740 yuan from the Shanghai fundraising for provincial flood emergency relief committee, and 476,566 yuan and 87 cents donated by various charitable organizations and philanthropists, plus 5,019 yuan and 5 cents in interest from various banks, totaling 1,266,325 yuan and 92 cents in ocean silver. A total of 1,194,176 yuan and 22 cents was allocated to various counties for emergency winter relief and to prepare relief grain and clothing. A subsidy of 10,600 yuan was allocated to the Shanghai shelter and the war zone refugee relief committee, 15,216 yuan and 72 cents for transportation, advertising, and the purchase of supplies, 23,399 yuan and 50 cents for the expenses of various county investigation and release bureaus, and 9,706 yuan and 66 cents for the association's expenses and compensation, totaling 1,253,099 yuan and 10 cents. Commissioner Cheng proposed that the association has done its best in emergency winter relief. With the approaching spring famine, relief is even more urgent. In addition, many refugees have returned from the war zone. Gao Bao, Xingtai, Dongtai, and other counties are full of refugees. These people are both hungry and homeless, and they have nowhere to escape. The miserable situation is beyond words. He has witnessed it with his own eyes and feels deeply distressed. He knows that it is difficult to raise funds in the current national crisis. It is beyond our ability to talk about spring relief. Can we raise a small amount of relief funds and do some work relief in an impossible situation, in order to make up for it in the event of an emergency? (Public Resolution) In the current national crisis, there is really no way to raise funds. We will send telegrams to various investigation and release bureaus to urge them to submit their relief sales and end the association's affairs as soon as possible.

US Court Continues Hearing of Crowley's Smuggling Case 20

Testimony of Gu Ziman, Anderly, and Keller

The *Great American Evening News* reported that the case of American Crowley being accused of smuggling opium to the United States was heard again yesterday (12th) afternoon by the US court. Mick Henry, an officer from the US transport ship *Garland*, testified. The prosecutor then summoned Gu Ziman, a waiter in the transport ship's galley at the time, who testified that on September 12th, he took a piece of paper and gave it to Mick Henry. Mick Henry then used it to wrap a package and told him to place it on the transport ship's freight car parked next to the pier. This morning (13th), the US court continued the hearing. First, the defendant's lawyer cross-examined Gu Ziman, and then summoned Anderly, a sea gate guard at the transport ship dock at the Mason Fort in San Francisco, who testified that that morning, he was sitting on the transport ship's freight car and saw a Filipino wearing a white chef's vest put a package on the car. The Filipino greeted him and hurried back to the transport ship. He waited for a long time in the car, but the owner of the item did not come, so he became suspicious and opened the package to see that there was a bottle of whiskey and eleven small packages, each packaged with five tin cans. He poked a can with a small knife, and it was filled with black material. He smelled it and there was no different smell. He tasted it and it tasted bitter. He tried to put a little bit on the wrapping paper and burned it, and he smelled the smell of opium. He re-wrapped it and immediately reported it to his superior, Lieutenant Jack. Later, he handed the package to the customs warehouse officer. He also said that he had testified in court during the military trial of Mick Henry, and Mick Henry was sentenced to five years in prison. Next, Keller, the manager of the Pacific Telegraph Company, testified, submitting the original drafts of telegrams between the defendant and the United States from June to October last year. After the testimony, he left the court.

Latest News on the *Shishi Xinbao* Labor Dispute 21

General Meeting of *Shishi Xinbao* Employees

Various Industry Unions Issue Declarations

Shanghai Fifth District Cigarette Industry Union, Fifth District Shipbuilding Union, Fifth District Paper Union, Fifth District Loading and Unloading Union, Fifth District Match Union, Fifth District Cotton Textile Union, Fifth District Basket Carrier Union, Fifth District Carpenter Union, Fifth District Cotton Spinning Union, Fifth District Civil Ship Repair Union, Fifth District Winery Union, etc., April 13th.

Postal Workers' Unions Report on the Mediation of the *Shishi Xinbao* Dispute 22

Reasons for Mediation: Since the *Shishi Xinbao* dispute occurred, our unions feared that the economic downturn would increase unemployment, and that the fledgling news industry would be hit, especially at this time of national crisis, when the labor and capital forces were divided, it would be impossible to complete the long-term resistance strategy. Therefore, one party issued a declaration to arouse social public opinion to promote labor-capital harmony and mutual assistance, and the other party came forward to mediate and exert patriotic enthusiasm to move labor and capital to be open and honest. People are not wood or stone, and they should be able to solve it easily. This is why our unions came forward to mediate.

Process of Mediation: On April 9th, our union representatives Zhu Xuefan and Huang Gongfu first sought the opinions of the newspaper industry union, and then went to *Shishi Xinbao*, where they were received by Manager Xiong Shaohao. Mr. Xiong sincerely described the cause of the dispute and the two-day grace period for filling out the application form. It is a pity that we could not meet Mr. Xiong on the 10th. On the 11th, it was not until 6 p.m. that we were able to contact Mr. Ren Ping, who was appointed by the newspaper. We accepted Mr. Ren's sincerity and accepted and considered the mediation opinions of our union, and agreed to talk with Mr. Zhang Zhuping, the person in charge of the newspaper, in person at 2 p.m. on the 12th. As a result of the talk on the 12th, our union's mediation was accepted, and our union's opinion was agreed to be answered on the evening of the 9th. At 11 p.m., Mr. Ren was entrusted by Mr. Zhang to contact us, saying that whether or not to restore the state before April 2nd required the opinion of the employees who had filled out the application form and entered the museum to work on the 13th at 11 a.m. to be accepted. At 1 p.m. on the 13th, Mr. Ren was again entrusted by Mr. Zhang to say that because the employees who had filled out the application form and entered the museum to work objected, it was difficult to accommodate the restoration of the previous state. Our union therefore knew that the mediation could not continue, so we notified the above situation to the labor side. This is the factual process of the mediation.

Mediation Opinions: Our union saw the *Shishi Xinbao*'s notice, knowing that workers could enter the museum by filling out an application form, and also received a letter from the labor side, knowing that the labor side's opinion was that the museum should apologize to the union, punish the museum's private arrest of union personnel in this case, compensate the losses suffered by the union this time, and restore the state before April 2nd. After our mediation, the union accepted the following opinions as a mediation method in order to relieve the anxieties of the people. (1) In order to maintain the discipline of the museum, workers should fill out application forms as a matter of course. (2) In order to protect the order set by the labor side (the museum can send a letter to the third party, stating that the union contract) the contract continues to be effective (the letter is kept by the third party). (3) Both sides restore the state before April 2nd.

Understanding of Mediation: The word strike was not ordered by the union. (A) According to the attachment to the museum's letter, the so-called union notice only specified that the union did not agree to the printing of *Da Wan Bao*, so it could not be printed privately. It can be seen that the union did not intend to strike in advance. (B) According to the talks between Mr. Xiong Ren and Mr. Jiang Jiemin himself, the curator Jiang of the museum did have a dispute with the committee member Zhang of the union at the time, and he indicated that he would twist him to the public bureau. According to the museum's letter, there was (the order was chaotic for a while, and the work was stopped. Later, the union sent people to gather all the employees and leave the museum). It can be seen that the employees' leaving the museum and the curator Jiang's improper handling were the reasons for promoting it. (C) According to the museum's letter, 5 o'clock is the time for typesetting advertisements on weekdays, and no employees returned to the museum. At 8 o'clock, it is the time for typesetting news on weekdays, and no employees came to work. Waiting until 9 o'clock, the museum only had accumulated manuscripts, and there was still no employee. The museum saw this situation and surmised that other employees were forced to strike. According to the responsible person of the museum, the museum reported to the police according to secret reports, fearing that the labor side would destroy the capitalists' property, and used force to protect it. At the same time, according to the responsible person of the labor side, the labor side did not enter the museum to work because it feared that the museum would hinder the workers' freedom movement, and at about 10 o'clock, the workers went to inquire about the news, but they were detained in the museum by the police force of the museum. According to the above facts and the union's declaration, it can be proved that the union did not order a strike. (D) The contradiction in the museum's restoration of administrative power. According to the responsible person of the museum, the museum's administrative power on weekdays was often hampered by the union, so it took this opportunity to make it a prerequisite for workers to fill out application forms and obey the museum's regulations. Our union also thought this reason was quite acceptable, so we had the first opinion. Unexpectedly, the museum could not accept the method of restoring the state before April 2nd because the employees who had filled out the application form and entered the museum to work objected, which was unavoidable.

A few concluding words: In short, our union does not want workers to lose their jobs, nor do we want the news industry to be destroyed, and we do not want internal conflicts to occur during the national crisis, which would increase the arrogance of the Japanese. All the mediation opinions are an expression of impartiality, and the labor side is willing to sacrifice everything, just to ensure that the employees do not lose their jobs. Still unable to get the understanding of the other party, the success has failed. I can only blame myself for not being sincere enough to move people, and not being righteous enough to impress the public. The mediation is temporarily suspended. If there is an opportunity for compromise in the future, and our union needs to contribute to it, then what can our union say? I hope people from all walks of life can teach us. Shanghai Postal Workers Union, Shanghai Postal Workers Union.

Lin Fengwen et al. Appeal the Sheng Family Inheritance Case 23

Sheng Zecheng et al. Also File an Appeal

The Debate Has Concluded and the Judgment Is Scheduled to Be Announced

Sheng Zecheng, Pinchen, Panchen, daughters Guan Yi, Fang Yi, Ai Yi, Jing Yi, and grandsons Yu Chang and Yu You, sons of the late Sheng Xuanhuai, were jointly sued by nephews Lin Fengwen and Lin Fengjun for encroaching on the inheritance. Sheng Zechen et al. argued that the Lin brothers had no right to inherit the inheritance and also filed a counterclaim requesting that the plaintiffs be prosecuted for false accusations. After investigation by the First Special District Court, the result was that both parties' accusations were not established, and the judgment was given that they were not guilty. Lin's private lawsuit for analyzing the inheritance was transferred to the civil court for handling. After the judgment, both parties claimed to be dissatisfied and filed separate appeals. Yesterday afternoon, the Criminal Court President Zhou Han of the First Special Court and two judges opened a court session to hear the case, ordering both parties to state their reasons for dissatisfaction. First, Lin Fengwen stated, "My mother's name is Xiao Yi, and she is the third daughter of Duke Bao. My mother gave birth to my two brothers. My mother died when I was only six months old. It has been thirty-five years now. The inheritance I am now requesting is owned by Madame Zhuang, and amounts to approximately three million. Divided among my mother's ten brothers and sisters, I should get 300,000. The inheritance is divided into two types: one is real estate, such as houses, etc., and the other is personal property, such as precious ornaments, antiques, etc. They were all divided up behind closed doors by the defendants and appellants on October 31st last year, and they even encroached on the share that I should inherit. The will they presented is a forgery. Therefore, I am not satisfied with the first instance's judgment that the defendants are not guilty, so I am filing an appeal." Presiding Judge Zhou then threw the will of Madame Zhuang to Lin for review because the will only mentioned that the four, five, six, and eight daughters would each receive 10,000 yuan and did not mention the appellant. Then, Sheng Zecheng, the mother of Lin Fengwen, is the third concubine of my half-brother. I am the son of Madame Zhuang. Madame Zhuang's inheritance is approximately 800,000, which has already been analyzed according to the will. Lin Fengwen has no right to enjoy this inheritance, but he filed a false accusation. I am not satisfied with the first instance's judgment that he is not guilty, so I am filing a special appeal." Next, Sheng Pinchen stated, "Fengwen was raised by my late parents from a young age. Unexpectedly, he has now filed a false accusation, which has a great impact on the world's morality and human heart. This point should be noted." Sheng Yu Chang and Yu You also successively stated that the accusation of encroaching was actually false. The three ladies Sheng Guan Yi, Fang Yi, and Jing Yi all stated that they each received 10,000 yuan in accordance with the will. They were not managers of the inheritance and were not responsible for the encroachment. However, they were also sued for encroachment, which was a false accusation, so they filed a special appeal, requesting that they be prosecuted for false accusations. However, Sheng Ai Yi said that because she was born to Madame Zhuang, she received 200,000 yuan when the inheritance was analyzed, but she was not in charge of the inheritance at the beginning, and the accusation of encroachment was a false accusation. Before Lin filed the lawsuit, he claimed that he needed to get married and run a business, and asked to borrow 30,000 yuan. Although he agreed to ask his brothers to say something, Lin suddenly filed a lawsuit, so it was inconvenient to continue the matter, etc. Finally, the lawyers of both parties debated with each other. The debate concluded, and Presiding Judge Zhou announced that the debate in this case was concluded, and the judgment would be announced on the afternoon of the 19th of this month.

Lung Hospital Establishes Civilian Treatment Department 24

The Shanghai Lung Disease Sanatorium at No. 2 Daxi Road in this city is a specialized hospital for treating tuberculosis. In view of the recent rapid increase in the number of residents in Shanghai, many patients are unable to carry out isolation and treatment due to economic difficulties, which is worrying. The medical director of the hospital, Dr. Ding Huikang, specially discussed with the hospital director, Mr. Huang Hanzhi, and decided to set aside part of the third hospital as a civilian treatment department, charging from one yuan per day. It is now ready and will begin to receive patients from today.

Doctor Yang Yanhe's Talk on Hygiene and Disease Prevention 25

Doctor Yang Yanhe of No. 80, Anshun Lane, Kangti Road, has considerable experience with febrile diseases and seasonal epidemics. According to Mr. Yang, "After a great war, there is sure to be a great plague," as the ancients have warned. Although that time has not yet arrived, this year's measles and smallpox often lead to pneumonia with rapid breathing and nasal flaring. Wind-heat combined with dampness often results in chest congestion and a greasy tongue, with the illness dragging on persistently, which are all signs of it. For prevention, it is advisable to stay in high, dry, and well-ventilated places, frequently sprinkling carbolic acid water. In low-lying, damp, and confined areas, frequently fumigate with Atractylodes lancea and Dahurian angelica root. Carry sweetgrass and spikenard, or camphor balls, with you. It would be even better if you could soak Dryopteris crassirhizoma in a water tank for drinking, and burn frankincense and benzoin in a censer to create a fragrant atmosphere. It is also important to be careful about daily life, moderate diet, and adjust to the temperature to maintain the body's resistance. It is best to abstain from meat such as fish, shrimp, pork, and beef.

Publication of "Collected Speeches of Modern Celebrities" 26

"Collected Speeches of Modern Celebrities" is compiled by Wang Weiyin, the president of the Sino-Foreign Academic Research Society. The entire book is divided into sections on party politics, education, industry, economics, literature, philosophy, youth, municipal administration, and other important issues. The material is novel, practical, and conveniently categorized for easy reading. It is truly a valuable resource for people in political, business, and academic circles to study and learn from. The book is now published and available at the Civilization Bookstore on Damalu Road and the Modern Bookstore on Simalu Road.

Weather Report 27

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the Shandong coast would be cloudy with a northeast wind. The Yellow Sea would have variable winds. The Yangtze River basin and the coast here would be overcast with rain or dew in some areas, due to a low-pressure system in southwestern China. The East China Sea and the Taiwan Strait would have northeast winds and rain. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the local temperature reached a high of 64.4 degrees and a low of 47.5 degrees. Last Sunday, the high was 68.0 degrees and the low was 41.7 degrees.

Regarding the Secret Agreement on Parallel Railway Lines 33

(Beiping) The memorandum prepared by the Chinese delegation, except for the issue of parallel railway lines in the Eastern Provinces, has been completed and submitted to Lytton. The Japanese are using the attachment to the secret agreement signed with Prince Qing in 1905 as a pretext for the issue of parallel railway lines in the Eastern Provinces. When the Investigation Commission passed by, the Japanese side showed it to them. It is said that the Japanese side was very secretive at the time, claiming that the Chinese had already lost it. It took a very long time to retrieve it from an iron box. The members of the Investigation Commission were quite impatient. Therefore, when the commission returned to the capital from Hankou, they were invited to disembark and shown the original agreement. Now both sides have sent photographic copies to the Investigation Commission. The commission has entrusted the embassy to carefully translate it. It is said that although the attachment mentioned that the Sino-Belgian treaty stipulated that parallel railway lines should be built more than 100 li apart to be considered very satisfactory, the existing railways in the three Eastern Provinces that run parallel to the South Manchuria Railway are on average more than 200 li apart and do not violate the treaty. Moreover, this attachment was never formally signed, so whether it can be considered legal is still questionable. The reason for the intense debate between the two sides lies here. (Special dispatch on the 13th)

National Crisis Conference Passes Important Resolutions 47

Requesting the government to withdraw punishment of Zhang Xueliang

(Luoyang) The National Crisis Conference held its sixth general meeting at the Xigong Conference Hall at 8:00 AM on the 12th. Sixty-four members attended, including twenty members of the Central Committee, two heads of the National Government Yuan and Ministries, and eleven observers. The meeting was chaired by Gao Yihan. The following items were discussed: (1) The case of reorganizing military discipline. This case was presented by the Defense and Pacification Review Committee after organizing and summarizing the proposals of Member Liu Tong and Member Wang Xingzhou. It was resolved and passed. (2) Member Zhang Juping and others proposed that the National Government immediately remove Zhang Xueliang from office and investigate him for losing territory and disgracing the country, and that the Military Affairs Commission properly dispose of his troops in order to recover the lost territory in the Northeast. It was resolved and passed. (3) The case of promoting local autonomy. This case was presented by the Pacification Review Committee after reviewing and revising the proposal of Member Wang Guangqiang. It was resolved and passed in accordance with the review opinion and sent to the government for adoption and implementation. (4) Honorary Chairman Zhangjia Hutuktu proposed a temporary motion to improve military, political, religious, and educational affairs in Mongolia and Tibet to resist foreign aggression. It was resolved and passed and sent to the government for adoption and implementation. (5) Various cases regarding disaster relief. This case was presented by the Disaster Relief Review Committee after reviewing sixteen proposals from the meeting and summarizing them into the following five cases: (A) Improving disaster relief administration, (B) Building water conservancy projects, (C) Immigrating and cultivating wasteland, (D) Developing agriculture, forestry, and small industries, (E) Managing food for the people. It was resolved and passed in accordance with the review opinion, and the temporary motion of Member Liu Weir such as please dredge rivers to relieve disasters was included in this case and sent to the government for adoption and implementation. (6) Various cases regarding economic construction. It was resolved to pass in accordance with the review opinion and sent to the government for adoption and implementation. (7) In order to facilitate pacification, please vigorously implement autonomy and improve autonomous measures to eliminate disasters and chaos and consolidate the foundation of the country. It was resolved to send to the government for reference. (8) Improve military and political affairs to facilitate the suppression of bandits and resistance against foreign aggression. It was resolved to send to the government for attention. (9) In the suppression of communists and the restoration of counties and cities, the system of equal land rights should be implemented immediately in order to eliminate the communist scourge as soon as possible. It was resolved to send to the government for consideration and adoption, and detailed measures should be formulated and implemented. (10) A. Implement military and civilian separation of powers, promote the spirit of justice, and establish the basic case for pacification. B. Adopt ideological guidance and good policies to fundamentally correct people's hearts and actively eliminate communist bandits. C. In order to quell the communists and discuss plans, the policy of suppression should be improved and changed to pacification, and kindness should be used to subdue people and save military strength. It was resolved that the above three cases should be sent to the government for adoption and implementation. (11) Please request the government to abolish all special criminal laws immediately and declare that from the Republic of China Fifteen years onwards, all past, present, and future criminal offenders, except for active-duty soldiers, shall be transferred to the courts for processing, in order to conform to the spirit of the five-power separation. It was resolved to send to the government for reference. (12) Please request the government to order all counties in the country to form defense regiments within a time limit and implement the Baojia system to eliminate banditry and assist in national defense. It was resolved to send to the government to order all provinces to implement it faithfully. (13) The Defense and Pacification Review Committee reported that in addition to reporting the results of successive reviews to the conference for discussion, there were 38 proposals submitted by various members, and it was proposed to forward them to the government for reference. In addition, other proposals that did not meet the procedures and various construction books and opinions all have points that can be adopted, and it is requested to attach them for reference. It was resolved to pass in accordance with the review opinion and send to the government for reference. (14) Thoroughly reform the navy and rectify customs to resist violent Japan. It was resolved to send to the government for adoption and implementation. (15) The declaration of this conference. It was resolved to pass it and have the presidium organize the text for publication. The meeting adjourned at 9:50 AM. (Central News Agency telegram on the 12th)

National Crisis Conference Sends Four Cables 48

Commending the People of Shanghai and Overseas Chinese

Encouraging Representative Yan and Soldiers of the Nation

(Luoyang) The National Crisis Conference sent the following cables on the 12th: (1) To comfort Representative Yan Huiqing, (2) To commend overseas Chinese for donating money to save the country, (3) To commend the people of Shanghai, (4) To encourage the soldiers of the nation. The original texts are recorded separately as follows:

To comfort Representative Yan Please forward to Representative Yan Huiqing from the Nanjing Ministry of Foreign Affairs. During this League of Nations conference, you negotiated and deliberated, worrying day and night, and were able to proclaim the world's righteousness and win international sympathy. Your diplomatic efforts are no less than fighting on the front lines. We are heartbroken by the national crisis and gather in the capital. We look up to your contributions from afar and deeply admire you. We send this telegram to comfort your hard work and hope that you will continue to fight and turn the tide. The country and the nation rely on you. National Crisis Conference Presidium Wang Xiaolai, Gao Yihan, Liu Hengjing, Tong Guanqian, Zang Qifang and all members.

Commending Overseas Chinese To all overseas Chinese in various ports, Over the years, there have been disasters and famines in the country, and our overseas Chinese have been known for their generosity in providing financial assistance. Recently, due to the increasing foreign aggression, you have donated funds to purchase weapons, raising more than tens of millions, which shows your patriotic enthusiasm. This conference is deeply grateful for your solidarity in times of crisis. We send this telegram to commend you and hope that you will continue to support the motherland with practical strength. (Same title as above)

Commending the people of Shanghai To all groups, people, and volunteer armies in Shanghai, Our soldiers in Songhu fought bravely for more than a month to defend territorial sovereignty, and their spirit of sacrifice shocked the world. And all sectors of our Shanghai compatriots have either exhausted their wealth or donated everything they have, and their material and spiritual assistance is a manifestation of national will, making the strong neighbor know that our people cannot be bullied and our country cannot be destroyed. The revival of the Chinese nation depends on this. In the midst of deep wounds and pain, we are filled with respect for the patriotic enthusiasm of our compatriots. We send this telegram to comfort and encourage you, and hope that you will continue to work hard to win the final victory. (Slightly abbreviated title)

Encouraging the soldiers of the nation To all commanders-in-chief, army commanders, division commanders, and all soldiers, The violent Japan, with its power, first occupied Liaoning, Jilin, Harbin, and Heilongjiang, and then disturbed Songhu. The situation is serious and there is no room for complacency. This conference believes that the way to save the country is to unite and rise up. In this autumn of power struggles, defending the country depends on the soldiers of the nation fulfilling their duties. Now, we sincerely offer four points: (1) End internal strife forever and resist foreign aggression. First, stop fratricide. If the nest is overturned, there will be no whole eggs. At this time when the enemy's troops are deeply entrenched, we must unite sincerely and work together to survive. Differences of opinion and conflicts of interest should all be eliminated with the goal of saving the nation. (2) Fight for a long time, endure hardship and be determined. Things are difficult, and we must fill the sea and move mountains. Our ambition is only to advance. The revival of Yue by Goujian and the resistance of Greece by Turkey are all examples of achieving final victory with the greatest determination. They rely on material, we rely on will. They seek speed, we benefit from persistence. We would rather sacrifice than surrender. For example, in the Battle of Songhu, our patriotic soldiers did well. (3) Absolutely obey the orders of the highest commander. The army was defeated in Xiangzhou because there was no commander. On the verge of fighting, we succeeded in facing the water. Relying on each other and acting like arms and fingers can we respond to the enemy. Talking about war without effective command, delaying efforts, wasting money and grain, and missing opportunities, how can we act as a shield and how can we face the people? Our loyal and brave soldiers must not do this. (4) Maintain the overall unity of finance, and advance both affairs and achievements. Military and political affairs should be separated, and we should abide by the law and be honest. Public and military affairs are the same. If we intercept national taxes in the name of military expenses, destroying the administrative system, or following in the footsteps of warlords, the financial future will be obstructed and the danger will increase, which our patriotic soldiers cannot bear. These four points are a rough outline. In the face of national crisis, it is a matter of life and death. The line between survival and destruction lies in one heart. We must revive the national spirit and be the vanguard of the people. May all our armed compatriots strive for it. (Slightly abbreviated title) (Central News Agency telegram on the 12th)

Japanese Military Train Derails on the China Eastern Railway 49

Explosives Explode and the Train Overturns

13 Dead and 50 Injured

(Beiping) Foreign telegram, A military train fully loaded with troops from the Domon Division derailed near the east of Harbin. Three Japanese soldiers died and eleven were seriously injured. (Special dispatch on the 13th)

(Harbin) According to the Domon Division Headquarters, a military train of the ○ unit returning to Harbin on the eastern line of the China Eastern Railway was derailed at 10:45 PM last night at a point fifteen kilometers east of Harbin by unknown persons who removed the rails, causing the locomotive to overturn along with the train and causing a fire. Fourteen people were killed, thirty-two were seriously injured, and many were slightly injured. (Electric News Agency telegram on the 13th)

(Harbin) The cause of last night's military train derailment has been determined to be the work of communist members instructed by a certain country. The communist members used tofu-shaped explosives used to destroy the Songhua River Bridge and installed them under the rails. The ○○ unit immediately took extraordinary precautions and is strictly pursuing the criminals. (Electric News Agency telegram on the 13th)

(Harbin) It is now known that in the train derailment, a total of fifteen Japanese officers and soldiers died, and a total of five train cars and forty-six freight cars were damaged. After the accident, a fire broke out in the car and burned the cars. Many horses were also killed in the car. (Reuters telegram on the 13th)

Page 8

(Tokyo) According to news from Harbin, a unit of Japanese soldiers left by train this morning and encountered an explosion and derailed at a point ten and a half miles east of Harbin, falling under a rock. Eleven soldiers died on the spot, nineteen were seriously injured, and some of them are not expected to survive, and seventy-four were slightly injured. The cause of the explosion is unknown, and the Japanese military authorities are now conducting a thorough investigation. (Reuters telegram on the 13th)

Commercial Transportation on the Chinese Eastern Railway Completely Stalled 55

Vehicle Problems Difficult to Solve

Serious Situation Feared

(Harbin) Currently, because Soviet Russia is moving Chinese Eastern Railway trains into Russian territory, export merchants cannot obtain sufficient freight cars to transport goods. The Chinese Eastern Railway Bureau must soon decide on one of the following three options: (1) Attempt to recover the trains, which is extremely difficult in the current situation. (2) Purchase new cars, which requires raising loans from foreign countries. (3) Convert the southern section of the Chinese Eastern Railway to narrow gauge so that trains from the South Manchuria Railway can be used, which would be equivalent to extending the South Manchuria Railway line to Harbin. If none of the above three options are approved by the Russian officials of the Railway Bureau, the new government of Manchuria will face an extremely difficult situation. It must either admit its inability to resolve this matter or devise another solution, and the result will be a very serious situation between the new government of Manchuria and the Soviet Union. As of April 5th, the Chinese Eastern Railway's funds and bank deposits totaled 11,750,000 Japanese yen, of which 9,834,000 yen was held in current accounts at the Far Eastern Bank and the Vladivostok National Bank, and the remaining funds were deposited in various Chinese and foreign banks. (13th Reuters Dispatch)

British Parliament Discusses Sino-Japanese Issue 56

Eden States British Position

(London) During this afternoon's session of the House of Commons, members raised many questions to the government about the situation in the Far East. Under-Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs Eden addressed the issue of the new government of Manchuria, stating that Foreign Secretary Simon had not expressed any opinion on the Japanese government's impending recognition of the new government of Manchuria. As far as he knew, the Japanese government's policy remained the same as that stated by the Foreign Secretary in response to questions in the House of Commons in February. At that time, the Foreign Secretary stated that the Japanese government would be more inclined to recognize this new country than any other government. Eden also stated that recognition was not related to the Open Door Policy, and that discussing this matter would not be beneficial. He had seen proclamations from Manchuria stating that the Open Door Policy might be subject to change, but the British position had already been clearly stated, and continuing to state it would not be beneficial unless there was direct evidence of harm to British interests. Eden also answered a question from Conservative MP Knox regarding the Japanese army's occupation of Chinese territory near Shanghai, stating that the Japanese 24th Mixed Brigade and 11th Division had been withdrawn to their home country in the second half of March. The Allied forces in Shanghai reported to League of Nations Secretary-General Drummond on March 21st that after a partial withdrawal of Japanese troops, there were still 37,000 troops. To his knowledge, this was the total number of Japanese troops currently stationed in Shanghai. Knox also mentioned Japan's desire to secure the safety of life and property of its residents, stating that last year Britain was willing to relinquish the rights of Britons in Shanghai, and asked whether Japan would increase its anxiety because of Britain's attitude, and whether Britain might make another (contribution) in the future. Eden replied that he felt it was unhelpful to discuss the merits of the dispute currently under negotiation. He could not say how far the negotiations would extend or to what extent they would need to continue before they concluded. (13th Reuters Dispatch)

Three Major International Conferences 83

Geneva, 12th (National Telegram) According to investigations by local authorities here, the total number of representatives from various countries here is over 100. This is because there are currently three conferences being held simultaneously: the Disarmament Conference, the League of Nations Council meeting, and the International Labor Conference. If the personnel of the various national delegations, including secretaries, are included, the number can reach five or six thousand. Geneva, a small place, suddenly adding so many people, feels quite overcrowded. A diplomat from a major European country expressed great regret about the outward clamor of Geneva, saying that while the outward appearance is like this, the content is really unfathomable. In recent months, the credibility of the League of Nations has been almost completely lost. The functions of the past have now been reduced to the extreme. Although representatives from all countries gather from all directions, it is just a matter of commotion and does not help the actual situation.

League of Nations Administrative Council 84

Chairman Tardieu Summarizes the Four-Power Conference

Finance Committee Report Decided to Re-Submit for Review

Geneva, 12th (National Telegram) The 56th session of the League of Nations Council opened this afternoon. French Prime Minister Tardieu, as chairman, first held a closed-door meeting to consider the agenda and discuss issues of a confidential nature. Then, an open meeting was held. Tardieu first delivered an opening speech, summarizing the London Four-Power Conference, saying that at that time, because the countries wanted to have the whole problem studied by experts again and then take practical steps, no agreement could be reached. The important agenda item of this session is the Finance Committee's report and its recommendation to lend to the four countries of Austria, Hungary, Greece, and Romania to avoid their financial collapse. British Foreign Secretary Simon began the discussion, questioning the effectiveness of further lending to the Danube states, because these states have been temporarily saved from financial difficulties by previous loans, but their burdens have become increasingly heavy, leading to today's predicament. German Vice Foreign Minister Pulo continued, tracing the cause of the Danube countries' predicament today to the peace treaty imposing impossible financial and economic conditions, which ultimately led to the unavoidable danger of bankruptcy, and asked the Council to pay attention to the Finance Committee's report, which emphasized that resolving the issues of reparations and war debts is of great importance to rescuing the Danube states. After Pulo's speech, the meeting adjourned and was scheduled to continue tomorrow morning.

Geneva, 12th (National Telegram) The League of Nations Council held a special meeting today to consider the financial problems of assisting Central European countries. French Prime Minister Tardieu immediately passed a resolution that representatives from the four countries of Britain, France, Italy, and Germany, which had failed to reach an agreement at the recent London conference, would meet with financial experts from the League of Nations to re-examine the report of the League of Nations Finance Committee, and then make a final decision on the method of assistance. It is now likely that the League of Nations Council will not be able to take any action to assist the fire-stricken finances of the Danube countries before the regular meeting on May 9th after this review, and general observers of current affairs even doubt whether the fundamental outlines can be agreed upon at an early date during the review, because the four countries sending representatives are limited to the four countries that failed to reach an agreement in London recently. The countries clearly know that the financial recovery of Central European countries is of great importance to them, but in order to safeguard their selfish national interests, a deadlock has been created, and it is now hoped that this deadlock can be broken through the mediation of League of Nations experts.

Geneva, 12th (National Telegram) At the League of Nations Council meeting this afternoon, two telegrams from Lord Lytton of the Lytton Commission of Inquiry were read. Finally, he said that if the authorities of Manchukuo made any further attempts to obstruct the work of the Commission of Inquiry, he would immediately report to the Council.

International Disarmament Conference 87

France Advocates Organizing International Army to Sanction Aggression

Proposes Complete Abolition of Lethal Weapons on Land, Sea, and Air

Geneva, 12th (National Agency) The General Committee of the International Disarmament Conference continued its general discussion this afternoon. Chairman Henderson, French Prime Minister Tardieu spoke, attacking the proposal made yesterday by U.S. representative Gibson to abolish tanks, cannons, and chemical warfare equipment, insisting that this proposal cannot solve the problem of disarmament. Only by implementing the French plan can an international authority with the power to sanction be created in the future. Finally, he warned the committee not to make merely immediate emergency resolutions. The committee then adjourned so that Tardieu could go to chair the League of Nations Council meeting.

Paris, 12th (Havas) Tardieu's speech at the Disarmament Conference said, in part, "If a country dares to violate the provisions of the Kellogg-Briand Pact, which renounce war as an instrument of policy, then it will be even more unbridled in regard to other secondary provisions, such as the prohibition of possessing or using certain ordnance. Therefore, a system of surveillance is indispensable, and sanctions are even more necessary. The reason why France's proposal advocates that whoever violates the pact should be judged as an aggressor is precisely for this reason. Abolishing ordnance in terms of substance not only fails to equalize the countries, but its nature is hypocritical and impractical, because no matter what kind of ordnance can be used for attack, it can also be used for defense, and vice versa, defensive ordnance can also be transferred to attack. To remedy this, preventing all wars is the only way. But to do so, the international organization must have the strongest weapons, and no country's military strength can exceed it. France's proposal follows the spirit of the Covenant, one side being prevention and the other being sanctions, seeking a method of practical guarantee, and its essence lies in this. This proposal is an active answer to the disarmament problem, and is not like those who advocate abolishing ordnance in substance, who are merely indulging in empty talk."

Geneva, 13th (Reuters) Italian Foreign Minister Grandi today advocated at the Disarmament Conference the complete abolition of heavy artillery, bomber aircraft, battleships, submarines, tanks, aircraft carriers, and germ warfare tactics. Grandi declared that the army, navy, and air force should abolish their most powerful weapons, which would make international aggression more difficult.

News Highlights

Counterfeit Country's Opium and Gambling Policies 90

Customs, Salt Revenues, and Postal Services Seized by the Japanese

The Counterfeit Country Will Rely on Opium and Gambling as its Lifeline

Northeast Transportation Rights Also Fall Entirely into Japanese Hands

Harbin Dispatch: All counterfeit policies of the Northeast counterfeit country are manipulated by the Japanese. The so-called counterfeit cabinet and counterfeit departments are merely empty shells. The customs, salt revenues, and postal services within the Northeast territory generate an annual income of over 80 million. Due to the urgent needs of the Japanese, the counterfeit country has openly dispatched personnel to take over in the name of the Manchukuo counterfeit country. However, the customs offices, due to their involvement in foreign debt guarantees, have refused to be taken over by foreign staff. In Shenyang, the counterfeit country's takeover commissioner, accompanied by Japanese troops, threatened to forcibly take over, leading to a customs closure in resistance. The Andong customs office and the Harbin customs office have also resisted in the same way, so the current system has been temporarily maintained. The Bank of China, where the salt revenues are deposited, has been repeatedly urged by the Japanese to have the counterfeit country withdraw the funds. The bank's branches within the Northeast territory are unable to cope and have responded by requesting a grace period. The Bank of China has telegraphed the Ministry of Finance for a solution. Until a solution is found, the bank has decided not to make any allocations. The situation in the post offices is similar to that of the customs offices. Foreign staff have refused to be taken over and have stated that they can only transfer control with an order from the Chinese government. The counterfeit country's commissioner has led multiple Japanese soldiers to the three general bureaus in Jilin, Shenyang, and Harbin for negotiations, but the results have been fruitless. The Japanese are eyeing the 30 million in postal revenue and are threatening to cut off postal communication. To maintain postal services, the post offices have submitted a request to the Ministry of Communications for instructions while suspending the acceptance of domestic remittances and insurance letters to avoid losses for mailers. It is rumored that two secretaries from the League of Nations investigation team have secretly come to the Northeast to conduct investigations into the aforementioned two matters. The Japanese are aware of this and have ordered a vigorous search for the whereabouts of the two secretaries to monitor their activities. The counterfeit country's current financial situation is dire due to the economic decline in various regions and the burden of supporting the Japanese military. (It is said that they must bear 3 million in Japanese military expenses each month.) Therefore, the Japanese are instigating the counterfeit country to implement new policies to increase revenue. One policy is opium monopoly, where the counterfeit customs will draft regulations to implement a monopoly on opium planting, with an estimated annual revenue of 20 million. The other policy is the construction of an international horse racing track in Changchun, with horse races and champagne lottery sales four times a year, also with an estimated revenue of 20 million. These two sources of revenue will be used to fund the counterfeit country's military and administrative expenses. The revenue from customs, salt, and postal services will be managed by the Japanese, ostensibly as trustees, but in reality, it will be completely swallowed by the Japanese.

The central bank that the Japanese are planning for the counterfeit country was originally intended to have a capital of 20 million Japanese yen, to be loaned by the Japanese. However, the Japanese have recently felt economic panic and are unable to provide this large sum. Therefore, they falsely claim that the Japanese government will not provide direct loans until it officially recognizes Manchukuo. Instead, Dongtuo, Mitsui, Mitsubishi, Mantetsu, and other companies will jointly lend 20 million silver dollars. In reality, these companies do not have such a large amount of cash for lending. Therefore, in the future, the Chosen Bank and the Yokohama Specie Bank may issue 20 million in gold notes to inject capital. The counterfeit central bank is scheduled to open on April 11, but the date is approaching, and there is no news, likely due to a lack of funds. According to the regulations of the counterfeit central bank drafted by the Japanese, there will be one governor and one comptroller. The governor will be Chinese, and the comptroller will be Japanese. However, all administrative expenditures must be signed by the comptroller to be valid. There will be seven directors, four Japanese and three Chinese, and five supervisors, two Japanese and three Chinese. Observing these numbers alone reveals where the power and responsibility of the counterfeit central bank lie. The position of counterfeit governor was originally intended to be filled by Pu Wei, but Pu Wei has his own agenda and is not cooperating with Pu Yi, so he is unlikely to accept the position. Therefore, there is news that it will be concurrently filled by Xi Qia.

Xi Qia is the number one meritorious official of the counterfeit regime, taking care of everything. In the counterfeit regime, he is considered second to none and above all others. Zheng Xiaoxu is nominally the counterfeit prime minister, but he is merely a messenger. Since Xi Qia has become complacent, Ma Zhanshan, Zang Shiyi, and others are quite resentful. Ma, due to his history of resisting Japan, is deeply resented by other traitors, who are trying to squeeze him out. Therefore, Ma is restless. He recently used an inspection as an excuse to take refuge in Baiquan in eastern Heilongjiang and refuses to return to the province. The counterfeit regime, fearing that this will trigger internal strife, has not hastily announced a replacement. Zhao Xinbo is the only favorite in front of Honjo Shigeru, but he has recently fallen out of favor because Zhao is involved in embezzlement. His position as mayor of Shenyang has been taken by the Japanese, who have appointed Yan Rentao, a former Dalian city councilor, to the position. Zhao has been promoted to the president of the counterfeit Legislative Yuan, but this is just an empty position, controlled entirely by the Japanese, and not as famous and profitable as the mayor's position. Therefore, Zhao is quite resentful and may refuse to take on the role of reception during the League of Nations investigation team's visit to the Northeast.

The various railways in the Northeast outstanding issues are currently being unilaterally resolved by the Japanese, who are constructing the Hu-Hai and Qi-Ke railways and having the counterfeit country sign agreements to transfer them to Mantetsu. The cost of the Qi-Ke railway is unknown, but the cost of the Hu-Hai railway is 6 million silver dollars. After the transfer, the Japanese will connect the tracks, linking the Qi-Ke and Hu-Hai railways into one line. These two railways were built with the blood and sweat of the people of Heilongjiang province for many years, and it is deeply regrettable that they have now been seized by the Japanese. (7th)
